				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bank of New York Mellon Corp.">The Bank of New York Mellon Corp.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<p><b>The Bank of New York Mellon Corporation</b> <b>BNY Mellon</b> is an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> worldwide <b>Banking</b> and <b>Financial</b> services holding company headquartered in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. Bank of New York was established in <b><a href="/wiki/1784" title="1784">1784</a></b>. BNY Mellon was formed  as a result of the merger of The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of New York">Bank of New York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mellon_Financial" title="Mellon Financial">Mellon Financial Corporation</a>. It is by far the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Custodian_bank" title="Custodian bank">custodian bank</a> and asset servicing company,<sup id="cite_ref-Teather06_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teather06-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick07_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick07-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tascarella07_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tascarella07-4">[4]</a></sup> with $1.9 trillion in <a href="/wiki/Assets_under_management" title="Assets under management">assets under management</a> and $35.8 trillion in assets under custody as of the third quarter of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10K2018_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K2018-1">[1]</a></sup> BNY Mellon is incorporated in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <a href="/wiki/US%24" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a> 362.87 billion <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="nowrap"><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <a href="/wiki/US%24" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a> 40.74 billion <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="nowrap">51,300 <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bnymellon.com">BNYMellon.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-10K2018_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K2018-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Through its Bank of New York predecessor, it is one of the three <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_banks_in_continuous_operation" title="List of oldest banks in continuous operation">oldest banking corporations</a> in the United States, and among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_banks_in_continuous_operation" title="List of oldest banks in continuous operation">oldest banks in the world</a>, having been established in June 1784 by a group that included American <a href="/wiki/Founding_Father" class="mw-redirect" title="Founding Father">Founding Father</a> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">Aaron Burr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe2011_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe2011-7">[7]</a></sup>  Mellon had been founded in 1869 by the <a href="/wiki/Mellon_family" title="Mellon family">Mellon family</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, which included Secretary of the Treasury <a href="/wiki/Andrew_W._Mellon" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew W. Mellon">Andrew W. Mellon</a>.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bank_of_New_York">Bank of New York</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Bank of New York" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waltonhouse.gif" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/be/Waltonhouse.gif" decoding="async" width="200" height="164" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="164"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 164px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/be/Waltonhouse.gif" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="164" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waltonhouse.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Walton Mansion housed the Bank of New York from 1784 to 1787.</div></div></div>
<p>The first bank in the U.S. was the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_North_America" title="Bank of North America">Bank of North America</a> in Philadelphia, which was chartered by the Continental Congress in 1781; <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Alexander Hamilton</a>, Thomas Jefferson and Benjamin Franklin were among its founding shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe2011_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe2011-7">[7]</a></sup> In February 1784, <a href="/wiki/BankBoston#The_Massachusetts_Bank" title="BankBoston">The Massachusetts Bank</a> in Boston was chartered.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe2011_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe2011-7">[7]</a></sup></p><p>The shipping industry in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> chafed under the lack of a bank, and investors envied the 14% dividends that Bank of North America paid, and months of local discussion culminated in a June 1784 meeting at a coffee house on <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Square_(Manhattan)" title="Franklin Square (Manhattan)">St. George's Square</a> which led to the formation of the Bank of New York company; it operated without a charter for seven years.  The initial plan was to capitalize the company with $750,000, a third in cash and the rest in mortgages, but after this was disputed the first offering was to capitalize it with $500,000 in gold or silver.  When the bank opened on June 9, 1784, the full $500,000 had not been raised; 723 shares had been sold, held by 192 people.  <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">Aaron Burr</a> had three of them, and Hamilton had one and a half shares.  The first president was <a href="/wiki/Alexander_McDougall" title="Alexander McDougall">Alexander McDougall</a> and the Cashier was William Seton.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1909_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1909-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jaffe14_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffe14-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hubbard1995_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hubbard1995-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hamilton1869_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hamilton1869-11">[11]</a></sup></p><p>Its first offices were in the old Walton Mansion in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-Teather06_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teather06-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT1909_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1909-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jaffe14_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jaffe14-9">[9]</a></sup>  In 1787, it moved to a site on <a href="/wiki/Hanover_Square_(Manhattan)" title="Hanover Square (Manhattan)">Hanover Square</a> that the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Cotton_Exchange" title="New York Cotton Exchange">New York Cotton Exchange</a> later moved into.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1909_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1909-8">[8]</a></sup></p><p>The bank provided the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> government its first loan in 1789. The loan was orchestrated by Hamilton, then <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Secretary of the Treasury">Secretary of the Treasury</a>, and it paid the salaries of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> members and <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rhodes_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rhodes-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>The Bank of New York was the first company to be traded on the New York Stock Exchange when it first opened in 1792.<sup id="cite_ref-NYA_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYA-13">[13]</a></sup>  In 1796, the bank moved to a location at the corner of <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street" title="Wall Street">Wall Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Street_(Manhattan)" title="William Street (Manhattan)">William Street</a>, which would later become <a href="/wiki/48_Wall_Street" title="48 Wall Street">48 Wall Street</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1909_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1909-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p><p>The bank had a monopoly on banking services in the city until the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_Manhattan_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of the Manhattan Company">Bank of the Manhattan Company</a> was founded by Aaron Burr in 1799; the Bank of New York and Hamilton vigorously opposed its founding.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT1909_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT1909-8">[8]</a></sup></p><p>During the 1800s, the bank was known for its conservative lending practices that allowed it to weather financial crises. It was involved in the funding of the <a href="/wiki/Morris_Canal" title="Morris Canal">Morris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erie_Canal" title="Erie Canal">Erie</a> canals, and <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">steamboat</a> companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Geisst09_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geisst09-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYARCH_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYARCH-16">[16]</a></sup> The bank helped finance both the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">Union Army</a> during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cox06_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox06-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RefBiz_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefBiz-18">[18]</a></sup> Following the Civil War, the bank loaned money to many major infrastructure projects, including utilities, railroads, and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Subway" title="New York City Subway">New York City Subway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geisst09_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geisst09-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>Through the early 1900s, the Bank of New York continued to expand and prosper.<sup id="cite_ref-NYARCH_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYARCH-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RefBiz_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefBiz-18">[18]</a></sup> In July 1922, the bank merged with the New York Life Insurance and Trust Company.<sup id="cite_ref-NYoldest_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYoldest-19">[19]</a></sup> The bank continued to profit and pay dividends throughout the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, and its total deposits increased during the decade.<sup id="cite_ref-NYARCH_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYARCH-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RefBiz_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefBiz-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1948, the Bank again merged, this time with the Fifth Avenue Bank, which was followed by a merger in 1966 with the Empire Trust Company.<sup id="cite_ref-Geisst09_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geisst09-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RefBiz_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefBiz-18">[18]</a></sup> The bank's <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> was created in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-Geisst09_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geisst09-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_new_york.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/71/Bank_of_new_york.png" decoding="async" width="140" height="140" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="140" data-file-height="140"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 140px;height: 140px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/71/Bank_of_new_york.png" data-alt="" data-width="140" data-height="140" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_new_york.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Older Bank of New York logo</div></div></div>
<p>In 1988, the Bank of New York merged with Irving Bank Corporation after a year-long <a href="/wiki/Hostile_take_over" class="mw-redirect" title="Hostile take over">hostile take over</a> bid by Bank of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>  Irving had been headquartered at <a href="/wiki/1_Wall_Street" title="1 Wall Street">1 Wall Street</a> and after the merger, this became the headquarters of the Bank of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p><p>From 1993 to 1998, the bank made 33 acquisitions, including acquiring JP Morgan’s Global Custody Business in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-RefBiz_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefBiz-18">[18]</a></sup> Ivy Asset Management was acquired in 2000, and the bank acquired Pershing LLC, the United States' second-largest trade clearinghouse,  in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-RefBiz_18-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefBiz-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TheStreet03_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheStreet03-22">[22]</a></sup></p><p>In 2005, the bank settled a US federal investigation that began in 1996 concerning <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> related to <a href="/wiki/Privatization_in_Russia" title="Privatization in Russia">post-Soviet privatization in Russia</a>.  The illegal operation involved two Russian emigres, one of whom was a Vice President of the bank, moving over US$7 billion via hundreds of wires.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>In 2006, the Bank of New York traded its retail banking and regional middle-market businesses for J.P. Morgan Chase's corporate trust assets. The deal signaled the bank's exit from retail banking.<sup id="cite_ref-ODonnell06_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ODonnell06-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Mellon_Financial">Mellon Financial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mellon Financial" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AWMellon.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/AWMellon.jpg/200px-AWMellon.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="263" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3158"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 263px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/AWMellon.jpg/200px-AWMellon.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="263" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AWMellon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Andrew W. Mellon</div></div></div>
<p>Mellon Financial was founded as T. Mellon &amp; Sons' Bank in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, Pennsylvania, in 1869 by retired judge <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mellon" title="Thomas Mellon">Thomas Mellon</a> and his sons <a href="/wiki/Andrew_W._Mellon" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew W. Mellon">Andrew W. Mellon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_B._Mellon" title="Richard B. Mellon">Richard B. Mellon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYJob_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYJob-26">[26]</a></sup> The bank invested in and helped found numerous industrial firms in the late 1800s and early 1900s including <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Westinghouse_Electric_(1886)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westinghouse Electric (1886)">Westinghouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Oil" title="Gulf Oil">Gulf Oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem_Steel" title="Bethlehem Steel">Bethlehem Steel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RefForBiz_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefForBiz-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown14_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown14-28">[28]</a></sup> Both Gulf Oil and Alcoa are, according to the financial media, considered to be T. Mellon &amp; Sons' most successful financial investments.<sup id="cite_ref-RefForBiz_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefForBiz-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brown14_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brown14-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>In 1902, T. Mellon &amp; Sons' name was changed to the Mellon National Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-RefForBiz_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefForBiz-27">[27]</a></sup> The firm merged with the Union Trust Company, a business founded by Andrew Mellon, in 1946.  The newly formed organization resulting from the merger  was named the Mellon National Bank and Trust Company, and was Pittsburgh's first US$1 billion bank.<sup id="cite_ref-Time46_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time46-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>The bank formed the first dedicated family office in the United States in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-Ashworth2015_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ashworth2015-30">[30]</a></sup> A reorganization in 1972 led to the bank's name changing to Mellon Bank, N.A. and the formation of a holding company, Mellon National Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-NYJob_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYJob-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RefForBiz_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefForBiz-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>Mellon Bank acquired multiple banks and financial institutions in Pennsylvania during the 1980s and 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In 1992, Mellon acquired 54 branch offices of <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Savings_Fund_Society" title="Philadelphia Savings Fund Society">Philadelphia Savings Fund Society</a>, the first savings bank in the United States, founded in 1819.<sup id="cite_ref-Quint1989_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quint1989-32">[32]</a></sup></p><p>In 1993, Mellon acquired The Boston Company from <a href="/wiki/American_Express" title="American Express">American Express</a> and AFCO Credit Corporation from The Continental Corporation. The following year, Mellon merged with the Dreyfus Corporation, bringing its mutual funds under its umbrella.<sup id="cite_ref-RefForBiz_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefForBiz-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1999, Mellon Bank Corporation became Mellon Financial Corporation. Two years later, it exited the retail banking business by selling its assets and retail bank branches to <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Financial_Group" title="Citizens Financial Group">Citizens Financial Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RefForBiz_27-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RefForBiz-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Merger">Merger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Merger" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On December 4, 2006, the Bank of New York and Mellon Financial Corporation announced they would merge.<sup id="cite_ref-Vries06_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vries06-33">[33]</a></sup> The merger created the world's largest securities servicing company and one of the largest asset management firms by combining Mellon’s wealth-management business and the Bank of New York’s asset-servicing and short-term-lending specialties.<sup id="cite_ref-Teather06_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teather06-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Vries06_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vries06-33">[33]</a></sup>  The companies anticipated saving about $700 million in costs and cutting around 3,900 jobs, mostly by attrition.<sup id="cite_ref-Teather06_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teather06-2">[2]</a></sup></p><p>The deal was valued at $16.5 billion and under its terms, the Bank of New York's shareholders received 0.9434 shares in the new company for each share of the Bank of New York that they owned, while Mellon Financial shareholders received 1 share in the new company for each Mellon share they owned.<sup id="cite_ref-Cox06_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox06-17">[17]</a></sup> The Bank of New York and Mellon Financial entered into mutual <a href="/wiki/Option_(finance)" title="Option (finance)">stock option</a> agreements for 19.9 percent of the issuer's outstanding <a href="/wiki/Common_stock" title="Common stock">common stock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vries06_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vries06-33">[33]</a></sup> The merger was finalized on July 1, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Tascarella07_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tascarella07-4">[4]</a></sup> The company's principal office of business at the One Wall Street office previously held by the Bank of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick07_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick07-3">[3]</a></sup> The full name of the company became The Bank of New York Mellon Corp., with the <b>BNY Mellon</b> brand name being used for most lines of business.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick07_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick07-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tascarella07_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tascarella07-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-merger_history">Post-merger history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Post-merger history" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2008, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Department of the Treasury">U.S. Treasury</a> named BNY Mellon the master custodian of the <a href="/wiki/Troubled_Asset_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Asset Relief Program">Troubled Asset Relief Program</a> (TARP) bailout fund during the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s financial crisis">financial crisis of 2007 to 2010</a>. BNY Mellon won the assignment, which included handling accounting and record-keeping for the program, through a bidding process.<sup id="cite_ref-Dash08_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dash08-34">[34]</a></sup> In November 2008, the company announced that it would lay-off 1,800 employees, or 4 percent of its global workforce, due to the financial crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-AP11_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP11-35">[35]</a></sup>  According to the results of a February 2009 <a href="/wiki/Stress_test_(financial)" title="Stress test (financial)">stress test</a> conducted by federal regulators, BNY Mellon was one of only three banks that could withstand a worsening economic situation.<sup id="cite_ref-Atal09_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atal09-36">[36]</a></sup> The company received $3 billion from TARP, which it paid back in full in June 2009, along with US$136 million to buy back <a href="/wiki/Warrant_(finance)" title="Warrant (finance)">warrants</a> from the Treasury in August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Bernard09_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bernard09-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stempel09_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stempel09-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2009, BNY Mellon purchased <a href="/wiki/Insight_Investment" title="Insight Investment">Insight Investment</a>, a management business for external funds, from <a href="/wiki/Lloyds_Banking_Group" title="Lloyds Banking Group">Lloyds Banking Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McGrath09_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGrath09-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AUM_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AUM-40">[40]</a></sup>  The company acquired <a href="/wiki/PNC_Financial_Services" title="PNC Financial Services">PNC Financial Services</a>' Global Investment Servicing Inc. in July 2010 and Talon Asset Management's wealth management business in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Zacks10_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zacks10-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stein11_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stein11-42">[42]</a></sup></p><p>By 2013, the company's capital had steadily risen from the financial crisis. In the results of the  Federal Reserve's <a href="/wiki/Dodd%E2%80%93Frank_Wall_Street_Reform_and_Consumer_Protection_Act" title="Dodd–Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act">Dodd-Frank stress test</a> in 2013, the bank was least affected by hypothetical extreme economic scenarios among banks tested.<sup id="cite_ref-Adler13_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adler13-43">[43]</a></sup> It was also a top performer on the same test in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Touryalai14_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Touryalai14-44">[44]</a></sup></p><p>BNY Mellon began a marketing campaign in 2013 to increase awareness of the company that included a new slogan and logo.<sup id="cite_ref-OLeary13_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OLeary13-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McMains13_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McMains13-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>In 2013, the bank started building a new IT system called <a href="/wiki/NEXEN_(platform)" title="NEXEN (platform)">NEXEN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Babcock15_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Babcock15-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Baliva16_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baliva16-48">[48]</a></sup> NEXEN uses open source technology and includes components such as an <a href="/wiki/Web_API" title="Web API">API</a> store, data analytics, and a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Boulton16-1_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boulton16-1-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fogarty16_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fogarty16-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2014, BNY Mellon sold its <a href="/wiki/1_Wall_Street" title="1 Wall Street">1 Wall Street</a> headquarters,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> and in 2015, moved into leased space at <a href="/wiki/Brookfield_Place_(New_York_City)" title="Brookfield Place (New York City)">Brookfield Place</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris14_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris14-52">[52]</a></sup> In June 2014, the company combined its global markets, global collateral services and prime services to create the new Markets Group,<sup id="cite_ref-Baert14_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baert14-53">[53]</a></sup> also known as BNY Markets Mellon.<sup id="cite_ref-globalinvestor_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalinvestor-54">[54]</a></sup> The company expanded its <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> office in October 2014 as part of the company's plans to grow its wealth management business.<sup id="cite_ref-Sender2014_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sender2014-55">[55]</a></sup></p><p>Between 2014 and 2016, BNY Mellon opened innovation centers focused on emerging technologies, big data, digital and cloud-based projects, with the first opening in <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Boulton14_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boulton14-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MacSweeney14_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacSweeney14-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Alois16_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alois16-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2017, BNY Mellon announced that it agreed to sell CenterSquare Investment Management to its management team and the private equity firm Lovell Minnick Partners. The transaction is subject to standard regulatory approvals and is expected to be completed by the end of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2018, BNY Mellon announced that it was again moving its headquarters location, less than four years after its prior move. The headquarters location was announced as 240 Greenwich Street, a renaming of the already BNY Mellon-owned 101 Barclay Street office building in <a href="/wiki/Tribeca" title="Tribeca">Tribeca</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> BNY Mellon had owned the office building for over 30 years, with control of the location obtained via 99-year ground lease. The same year, the company purchased the location from the city for $352 million.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_data">Historical data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Historical data" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>The following graphs represent the net income and assets and liabilities for the years 2000 to 2016 for the Bank of New York Mellon, the Bank of New York Mellon Corporation's New York state-chartered bank and an FDIC-insured depository institution.
</p><p><br></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>BNY Mellon operates in 35 countries in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe,_the_Middle_East_and_Africa" title="Europe, the Middle East and Africa">Europe, the Middle East and Africa</a> (EMEA), and <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific" title="Asia-Pacific">Asia-Pacific</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fleisher14_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fleisher14-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-66">[66]</a></sup> The company employed 51,300 people as of December 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-10K2018_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K2018-1">[1]</a></sup> In October 2015, the group's American and global headquarters relocated to <a href="/wiki/225_Liberty_Street" title="225 Liberty Street">225 Liberty Street</a>, as the former <a href="/wiki/1_Wall_Street" title="1 Wall Street">1 Wall Street</a> building was sold in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Morris14_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morris14-52">[52]</a></sup> In July 2018, the company changed its headquarters again, this time to its existing 240 Greenwich Street location in New York (previously addressed 101 Barclay St).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The group's EMEA headquarters are located in London and its Asia-Pacific headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jönsson09_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-J%C3%B6nsson09-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FundWeb_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FundWeb-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Business">Business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Business" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The bank's primary functions are managing and servicing the <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">investments</a> of institutions and <a href="/wiki/High-net-worth_individual" title="High-net-worth individual">high-net-worth individuals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYA_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYA-13">[13]</a></sup> Its two primary businesses are Investment Services and Investment Management,<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-70">[70]</a></sup> which offer services for each stage of investment, from creation through to trading, holding, management, distribution and restructuring.<sup id="cite_ref-CrunchBase14_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CrunchBase14-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boyars14_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyars14-72">[72]</a></sup> The bank's clients include 80 percent of Fortune 500 companies.<sup id="cite_ref-Amjaroen14_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amjaroen14-73">[73]</a></sup> The company also serves 77 percent of the top 100 endowments, 87 percent of the top 1,000 pension and employee benefit funds, 51 percent of the top 200 life and health insurance companies and 50 percent of the top 50 universities.<sup id="cite_ref-BNY_Mellon_CSR_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNY_Mellon_CSR-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Investment_Services">Investment Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Investment Services" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>The bank's Investment Services business represents approximately 72 percent of the company's revenue<sup id="cite_ref-BNYMellon15_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNYMellon15-75">[75]</a></sup>  and it has $31.1 trillion under its custody or administration as of September 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Singh17_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singh17-76">[76]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> offered by the business include asset servicing, <a href="/wiki/Alternative_investment" title="Alternative investment">alternative investment</a> services, <a href="/wiki/Broker-dealer" title="Broker-dealer">broker-dealer</a> services, <a href="/wiki/Corporate_trust" title="Corporate trust">corporate trust</a> services and <a href="/wiki/Treasury_services" title="Treasury services">treasury services</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-70">[70]</a></sup> Other offerings include global collateral services, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Securities_lending" title="Securities lending">securities lending</a>, middle and back office outsourcing, and <a href="/wiki/Depository_receipt" class="mw-redirect" title="Depository receipt">depository receipts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>The company's subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Pershing_LLC" title="Pershing LLC">Pershing LLC</a> handles securities services, including execution, settlement, and clearing. It also provides back office support to financial advisors.<sup id="cite_ref-PershingYahoo_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PershingYahoo-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters13_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters13-78">[78]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, the company formed a new Markets Group, which offers <a href="/wiki/Collateral_management" title="Collateral management">collateral management</a>, securities finance, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market" title="Foreign exchange market">foreign exchange</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capital_market" title="Capital market">capital markets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Baert14_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baert14-53">[53]</a></sup> The group is now known as BNY Mellon Markets.<sup id="cite_ref-globalinvestor_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalinvestor-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Investment_Management">Investment Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Investment Management" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>BNY Mellon's Investment Management business generates 28 percent of the company's revenue<sup id="cite_ref-BNYMellon15_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNYMellon15-75">[75]</a></sup> and had US$1.7 trillion (Q4 2016) in assets under management.<sup id="cite_ref-Keats16_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keats16-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2017-10-K_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2017-10-K-81">[81]</a></sup> It operates several asset management boutiques and as of 2014 was the largest <a href="/wiki/Boutique#Boutique_industries" title="Boutique">multi-boutique</a> investment manager in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Boyars14_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyars14-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Battersby14_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Battersby14-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>BNY Mellon's <a href="/wiki/Wealth_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="Wealth Management">Wealth Management</a> unit handles the private banking, estate planning, <a href="/wiki/Family_office" title="Family office">family office</a> services, and investment servicing and management of high-net-worth individuals and families.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Milburn14_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milburn14-83">[83]</a></sup> As of 2014, it ranks 7th among wealth management businesses in the United States. Starting in 2013, the unit began expansion efforts, including opening eight new banking offices, increasing salespeople, bankers, and portfolio managers on staff, and launching an awareness campaign for wealth management services through television ads.<sup id="cite_ref-Milburn14_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milburn14-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Leadership" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charles_W._Scharf" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles W. Scharf">Charles W. Scharf</a> was appointed CEO in July 2017 and became Chairman after former CEO and Chairman <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Hassell" title="Gerald Hassell">Gerald Hassell</a> retired at the end of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Bray17_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bray17-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mollenkamp11_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mollenkamp11-85">[85]</a></sup> Hassell had been Chairman and CEO since 2011, after serving as BNY Mellon's president from 2007 to 2012<sup id="cite_ref-Mollenkamp11_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mollenkamp11-85">[85]</a></sup> and as the president of the Bank of New York Mellon from 1998 until its merger.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Karen_Peetz" title="Karen Peetz">Karen Peetz</a> served as president (the bank's first female president) from 2013 to 2016, when she retired; the company did not appoint a new president when she retired.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Burns14_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burns14-88">[88]</a></sup> Thomas Gibbons served as CFO between 2008 and 2017, when he also serves as vice chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-Taub08_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Taub08-89">[89]</a></sup> In 2017, Gibbons was replaced as CFO by Michael P. Santomassimo.<sup id="cite_ref-NewCFO_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewCFO-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PIOnline_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIOnline-91">[91]</a></sup> BNY Mellon's Investment Management business is run by CEO Mitchell Harris,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> and the company's Investment Services business was led by Brian Shea<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters14_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters14-93">[93]</a></sup> until his retirement in December 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>As of July 2017, the company's board members were Linda Z. Cook, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_M._Donofrio" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas M. Donofrio">Nicholas M. Donofrio</a>, Joseph J. Echevarria, Edward P. Garden, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_A._Goldstein" title="Jeffrey A. Goldstein">Jeffrey A. Goldstein</a>, Gerald L. Hassell, John M. Hinshaw, Edmund F. (Ted) Kelly, <a href="/wiki/John_A._Luke_Jr." title="John A. Luke Jr.">John A. Luke Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Morgan" title="Jennifer Morgan">Jennifer Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_A._Nordenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark A. Nordenberg">Mark A. Nordenberg</a>, Elizabeth E. Robinson, Charles W. Scharf and Samuel C. Scott III.<sup id="cite_ref-BoD_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoD-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Company_culture">Company culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Company culture" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, BNY Mellon formed a Board of Directors corporate social responsibility committee to set sustainability goals.<sup id="cite_ref-Gell15_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gell15-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schaeffer14_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaeffer14-97">[97]</a></sup> The company's <a href="/wiki/Corporate_social_responsibility" title="Corporate social responsibility">corporate social responsibility</a> activities include <a href="/wiki/Philanthropy" title="Philanthropy">philanthropy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_finance" title="Social finance">social finance</a> in the communities the bank is located in, and protecting financial markets globally.<sup id="cite_ref-EssentialPittsburgh14_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EssentialPittsburgh14-98">[98]</a></sup></p><p>The bank's <a href="/wiki/Philanthropy" title="Philanthropy">philanthropic</a> activities include financial donations and volunteerism.<sup id="cite_ref-Grgurich13_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grgurich13-99">[99]</a></sup> The company matches employee volunteer hours and donations with financial contributions through its Community Partnership program.<sup id="cite_ref-Massello14_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Massello14-100">[100]</a></sup> Between 2010 and 2012, the company and its employees donated approximately $100 million to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-Grgurich13_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grgurich13-99">[99]</a></sup> In 2014, the company worked with the <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> Fund to create a platform that connects <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">nonprofit organizations</a> with private businesses to solve social challenges.<sup id="cite_ref-Tascarella14_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tascarella14-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>The company received a 100 A rating in 2013, 2014 and 2015 by the CDP, which measures corporate greenhouse gas emissions and disclosures.<sup id="cite_ref-Schaeffer14_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaeffer14-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EnviroLeader14_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EnviroLeader14-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Henry15_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henry15-103">[103]</a></sup>  BNY Mellon was named on the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Sustainability_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Dow Jones Sustainability Index">Dow Jones Sustainability North America Index</a> in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-JustMeans14_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JustMeans14-104">[104]</a></sup> 2014 and 2015, and the World Index in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-Clancy14_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clancy14-105">[105]</a></sup> 2015<sup id="cite_ref-Techsonian15_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Techsonian15-106">[106]</a></sup> and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-DJSI2016_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DJSI2016-107">[107]</a></sup>  Another one of the company's focuses has been building efficiency. As of 2014, the company has saved $48 million due to building efficiency. Five of its buildings have achieved <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design</a> (LEED-EB) certification and 23 have interiors that are LEED certified.<sup id="cite_ref-Schaeffer14_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schaeffer14-97">[97]</a></sup></p><p>The company has business resource groups for employees that are focused on diversity and inclusion.<sup id="cite_ref-EssentialPittsburgh14_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EssentialPittsburgh14-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Catalyst13_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalyst13-108">[108]</a></sup> In 2009, Karen Peetz co-founded the BNY Mellon Women’s Initiative Network (WIN), a resource group for female employees' professional development.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> As of 2013, WIN had 50 chapters.<sup id="cite_ref-Masud13_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Masud13-110">[110]</a></sup> Other groups include PRISM for <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> employees, IMPACT, which serves multicultural employees and HEART for employees with disabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Catalyst13_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Catalyst13-108">[108]</a></sup> The bank has services for returning military, including a tool to help veterans align military skills and training with jobs at the company.<sup id="cite_ref-DiversityJournal14_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DiversityJournal14-111">[111]</a></sup> In 2014, it was recognized for its diversity practices by the National Business Inclusion Consortium, which named it Financial Services Diversity Corporation of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-Affinity14_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Affinity14-112">[112]</a></sup></p><p>In 2009, the company began an innovation program for employees to suggest ideas for large-scale projects and company improvement. Ideas from the initial pilot program generated approximately $165 million in pretax profit. The program results in an annual contest called "ACE" in which teams pitch their ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-Milligan14_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milligan14-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies_and_legal_issues">Controversies and legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Controversies and legal issues" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_currency_exchange_issues">Foreign currency exchange issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Foreign currency exchange issues" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2011, the U.S. Justice Department and New York's attorney general filed civil lawsuits against the Bank of New York, alleging foreign currency fraud. The suits hold that the bank deceived pension-fund clients by manipulating the prices assigned to them for foreign currency transactions. Allegedly, the bank selected the day's lowest rates for currency sales and highest rates for purchases, appropriating the difference as corporate profit. The scheme was said to have generated $2 billion for the bank, at the expense of millions of Americans' retirement funds, and to have transpired over more than a decade. Purportedly, the bank would offer secret pricing deals to clients who raised concerns, in order to avoid discovery. Bank of New York defended itself vigorously, maintaining the fraud accusations were "flat out wrong" and warning that as the bank employed 8,700 employees in New York, any damage to the bank would have negative repercussions for the state of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_Civil_Suit_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_Civil_Suit-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harry_Markopolos_interview_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harry_Markopolos_interview-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2015, the company admitted to facts concerning the misrepresentation of foreign exchange pricing and execution. BNY Mellon's alleged misconduct in this area includes representing pricing as best rates to its clients, when in fact they were providing clients with bad prices while retaining larger margins. In addition to letting go key executives, the company agreed to pay a total of US$714 million to settle related lawsuits.<sup id="cite_ref-Gara14_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gara14-116">[116]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2015, BNY Mellon agreed to pay $180 million to settle a foreign exchange-related lawsuit.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2016, multiple plaintiffs filed suit against the bank, alleging that the company had breached its fiduciary duty to ERISA plans that held American Depositary Receipts by overcharging retirement plans that invested in foreign securities.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> In March 2017, the presiding judge declined to dismiss the suit. In December 2017, another lawsuit alleged that BNY Mellon manipulated foreign exchange rates was filed by Sheet Metal Workers’ National Pension Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> BNY Mellon agreed to pay $12.5 million to settle the 2016 lawsuit in December 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_data_breach">Personal data breach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Personal data breach" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In February 2008, BNY Mellon suffered a security breach resulting in the loss of personal information when backup tapes containing the personal records of 4.5 million individuals went missing. Social security numbers and bank account information were included in the records. The breach was not reported to the authorities until May 2008, and letters were sent to those affects on May 22, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2008, the number of affected individuals was raised to 12.5 million, 8 million more than originally thought.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="IT_system_outages">IT system outages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: IT system outages" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On Saturday, August 22, 2015, BNY Mellon's SunGard accounting system broke down during a software change. This led to the bank being unable to calculate <a href="/wiki/Net_asset_value" title="Net asset value">net asset value (NAV)</a> for 1,200 mutual funds via automated computer system.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Between the breakdown and the eventual fix, the bank calculated the values using alternative means, such as manual operation staff. By Wednesday, August 26, the system was still not fully operational.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The system was finally operational to regular capacity the following week. As a result of a Massachusetts Securities Division investigation into the company's failure and lack of a backup plan, the company paid $3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2016, another major technology issue caused BNY Mellon to be unable to process payments related to the <a href="/wiki/SWIFT" class="mw-redirect" title="SWIFT">SWIFT</a> network. As of the time of the issue, the bank processed about 160,000 global payments daily totally an average of $1.6 trillion.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-128">[128]</a></sup> The company was unable to process payments for a 19 hours, which led to a backlog of payments and an extension of <a href="/wiki/Fedwire" title="Fedwire">Fedwire</a> payment services.<sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Privately_owned_public_space_agreement_violation">Privately owned public space agreement violation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Privately owned public space agreement violation" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to a <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Comptroller" title="New York City Comptroller">New York City Comptroller</a> audit in April 2017, BNY Mellon was in violation of a <a href="/wiki/Privately_owned_public_space" title="Privately owned public space">privately owned public space (POPS)</a> agreement for at least 15 years. In constructing the 101 Barclay Street building in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Manhattan" title="Lower Manhattan">Lower Manhattan</a>, BNY Mellon had received a permit allowing modification of height and setback regulations in exchange for providing a lobby accessible to the general public 24 hours a day. Auditors and members of the public had been unable to access or assess the lobby for many years, and were actively prevented from doing so by BNY Mellon security.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2018, the company began to permit public access to a portion of the lobby.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> However, BNY Mellon remains in violation of its agreement, as the lobby must be accessible to the public 24 hours a day.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment_legal_issues">Employment legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Employment legal issues" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>BNY Mellon settled foreign bribery charges with the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> (SEC) in August 2015 regarding its practice of providing internships to relatives of officials at a Middle Eastern investment fund.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The U.S. SEC found the firm in violation of the Foreign Corrupt Practices Act.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> The case was settled for $14.8 million.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2019, BNY Mellon staff considered legal options after the company banned employees from working from home.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> In particular, staff cited concerns regarding the impact on childcare, mental health, and diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The company reverted the ban as a result of employee outcry.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_legal_issues">Other legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other legal issues" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In September 2009, BNY Mellon settled a lawsuit that had been filed against the Bank of New York by the Russian government in May 2007 for <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a>; the original suit claimed $22.5 billion in damages and was settled for $14 million.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes1_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes1-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnnmoney_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnmoney-140">[140]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> sued BNY Mellon for allegedly failing to adhere to the investment guidelines relating to the state’s pension fund. The company settled with the state in June 2013 for $34 million.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2012, BNY Mellon settled a class action lawsuit relating to the collapse of Sigma Finance Corp. The suit alleged that the bank invested and lost cash collateral in medium-term notes. The company settled the lawsuit for $280 million.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2018, BNY Mellon agreed to pay nearly $54 million to settle charges of improper handling of "pre-released" <a href="/wiki/American_depositary_receipt" title="American depositary receipt">American depositary receipts (ADRs)</a> under investigation of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC)</a>. BNY Mellon did not admit or deny the investigation findings but agreed to pay disgorgement of more than $29.3 million, $4.2 million in prejudgment interest and a penalty of $20.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition_and_rankings">Recognition and rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Recognition and rankings" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>As of 2015, BNY Mellon was the world's largest custody bank,<sup id="cite_ref-BNYMellon15_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BNYMellon15-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McLaughlin15_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McLaughlin15-146">[146]</a></sup> the sixth largest investment management firm in the world<sup id="cite_ref-Manning15_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manning15-147">[147]</a></sup> and the seventh largest wealth management firm in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Sender2014_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sender2014-55">[55]</a></sup>  In 2018, BNY Mellon ranked 175 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> and 250 on the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Times_Global_500" title="Financial Times Global 500">Financial Times Global 500</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dullforce14_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dullforce14-149">[149]</a></sup> It was named one of world's 50 Safest Banks by <i><a href="/wiki/Global_Finance_(magazine)" title="Global Finance (magazine)">Global Finance</a></i>  in 2013 and 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-Cunningham14_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cunningham14-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cunningham13_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cunningham13-151">[151]</a></sup> and one of the 20 Most Valuable Banking Brands in 2014 by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Banker" title="The Banker">The Banker</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wallace14_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wallace14-152">[152]</a></sup></p><p>The bank says it is the longest running bank in the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> and whether it deserves this recognition is sometimes disputed by its rivals and also by some historians.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe2011_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe2011-7">[7]</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_North_America" title="Bank of North America">Bank of North America</a> was chartered in 1781, and was absorbed by a series of other entities until it was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a>. Similarly, <a href="/wiki/BankBoston#The_Massachusetts_Bank" title="BankBoston">The Massachusetts Bank</a> went through a series of acquisitions and ended up as part of <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>.  The Bank of New York remained independent, absorbing other companies, until its merger with Mellon.  There is no doubt that the BNY Mellon is at least the third oldest bank in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-Globe2011_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globe2011-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorships">Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sponsorships" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>Since 2012, BNY Mellon has expanded its number of sponsorships.<sup id="cite_ref-IEG_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEG-154">[154]</a></sup> It is the title sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Boat_Club" title="Oxford University Boat Club">Oxford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_University_Boat_Club" title="Cambridge University Boat Club">Cambridge</a> <a href="/wiki/The_Boat_Race" title="The Boat Race">Boat Race</a> in London, which had been called the BNY Mellon Boat race from 2012 to 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-IEG_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEG-154">[154]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Long12_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Long12-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> The company also sponsors the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Charles_Regatta" title="Head of the Charles Regatta">Head of the Charles Regatta</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IEG_154-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEG-154">[154]</a></sup> In 2013, the company became a 10-year sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a> and a founding partner of <a href="/wiki/Levi%27s_Stadium" title="Levi's Stadium">Levi's Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Long1_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Long1-157">[157]</a></sup> The company is a regular sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Academy_of_Arts" title="Royal Academy of Arts">Royal Academy of Arts</a> in London.<sup id="cite_ref-LondonEvening13_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LondonEvening13-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Bank_of_New_York_Mellon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
